          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781408708989" href="/book/show/30030950-fantastic-beasts-and-where-to-find-them">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26439378-lauren?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1814300760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9235175083034068147">I absolutely loved this book!!! It was amazing and it was the perfect way to get another taste of the wizarding world. I don’t even know where to start. This book is based in the 1920s which is many many years before the time of Harry Potter. It was also based in America! Both these things gave us an insight into how everything was many years before and in a different country. The entire storyline was perfect and I wish that it was a proper book with more detail. <br/><br/>I watched the movie before the b</span>
  <span id="freeText9235175083034068147" style="display:none">I absolutely loved this book!!! It was amazing and it was the perfect way to get another taste of the wizarding world. I don’t even know where to start. This book is based in the 1920s which is many many years before the time of Harry Potter. It was also based in America! Both these things gave us an insight into how everything was many years before and in a different country. The entire storyline was perfect and I wish that it was a proper book with more detail. <br /><br />I watched the movie before the book and to be honest I recommend you do that. They are exactly the same but reading a script makes it very hard to visualize everything but because I watched the movie first I could picture everything so vividly. It felt like I was watching the movie all over again. I don’t particularly like reading scripts mainly because of what I said before but this script was quite descriptive. Originally I wasn’t going to watch the movie first but it kind of just happened and I don’t regret it. <br /><br />This book incredible but I know deep in my heart I will always love Harry Potter much more because let’s be honest here, nothing can beat Harry Potter. This book/movie is still so good and reading the script makes me want to go and watch the movie again!! I totally recommend everyone to read it even if they aren't a fan of HP.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9235175083034068147" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1942772247" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1942772247" />
    <a title="Barbara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2172096-barbara"><img alt="Barbara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1598060221p2/2172096.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1942772247?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara" href="/user/show/2172096-barbara">Barbara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1942772247" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16621200142643859538"><br/>This screenplay for the film "Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them" (a prequel to the Harry Potter books) is humorous and entertaining.<br/><br/>The story: It's 1926 and Newt Scamander, a magizoologist, arrives in New York City with a case full of magical creatures. Inadvertently, Newt steps into a sea of trouble.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552352563i/27191154.png' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552352563i/27191153.png' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552352563i/27191151.png' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The notorious dark wizard Gellert Grindelwald has been causing havoc all over the world, raising fears that 'no-mags' (muggles) will learn there are witches and wizards in their midst. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552352563i/27191152.png' alt='' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Thus Ne</span>
  <span id="freeText16621200142643859538" style="display:none"><br>This screenplay for the film "Fantastic Beasts and Where to Find Them" (a prequel to the Harry Potter books) is humorous and entertaining.<br><br>The story: It's 1926 and Newt Scamander, a magizoologist, arrives in New York City with a case full of magical creatures. Inadvertently, Newt steps into a sea of trouble.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552352563i/27191154.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552352563i/27191153.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552352563i/27191151.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The notorious dark wizard Gellert Grindelwald has been causing havoc all over the world, raising fears that 'no-mags' (muggles) will learn there are witches and wizards in their midst. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552352563i/27191152.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Thus New York based MACUSA (Magical Congress of the United States of America)* is working day and night to keep magical occurrences below the radar. To this end, Tina Goldstein (a demoted Auror) is scouring the city for sorcerous miscreants. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552353739i/27191225.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Several creatures escape from Newt's case and his 'Niffler' goes on a spree, stealing shiny objects and gold coins all over the place. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552353574i/27191211._SX540_.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>While trying to catch the Niffler, Newt accidentally exchanges cases with Jacob Kowalski - a no-mag, would-be bakery shop owner - who's drawn into Newt's hijinks. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552353574i/27191212.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Newt and Jacob attract the attention of Tina, who promptly arrests the duo and brings them to MACUSA headquarters. However, Newt has a deft hand with a wand - and needs to capture his escaped beasties - so the wizard soon engineers a 'prison break.' <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552353574i/27191213._SX540_.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Meanwhile, no-mag 'preacher' Mary Lou Barebone is sure there are witches and wizards around, and wants to expose and exterminate them. To this end she founds an organization called the 'New Salem Philanthropic Society' and proceeds to makes speeches and hold demonstrations around the city.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552353574i/27191214.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Add a mysterious black whirlwind that's destroying parts of New York and killing people.....and all the elements are in place for an exciting magical adventure.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552353574i/27191215._SX540_.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Other interesting characters in the story include: Newt's array of supernatural creatures.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552354553i/27191264.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552354553i/27191265.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552354553i/27191266.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> Tina Goldstein's sister Queenie - who's a legilimens (mind reader).<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552353574i/27191216._SX540_.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Mary Lou Barebone's three adopted children, Credence, Chastity, and Modesty - who (supposedly) help with her witch-eradication campaign.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552353574i/27191217.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552356150i/27191390.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552353574i/27191218.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Langdon Shaw, who's seen supernatural things and wants to tell the world; Langdon's brother, Senator Henry Shaw - a politically ambitious man who wants Langdon to go away and shut up; and more.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552353574i/27191219.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1552353574i/27191220._SX540_.png" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm a big fan of Harry Potter and I completely enjoyed this screenplay. Highly recommended to fans of the boy wizard.<br><br>*The term MACUSA (which I assume is a take-off on Yakusa) really cracked me up.<br><br>You can follow my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot.com/">http://reviewsbybarbsaffer.blogspot.com/</a></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3467635980" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5554459922210189719">First of all ... Newt Scamander I am in love with you. I was already in love with Eddie Redmayne and now this happened and <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1597466933ra/29969870.gif' width='1000' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>So ... <i>this book.</i><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468247919ra/19683415.gif' width='1000' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I loved the heck out of this. The magic is still there dude. I umm ... don't get along with Hufflepuffs (no offence to all the Hufflepuffs out there. I love you [even though i don't know you]. What i mean is the qualities of the Hufflepuff house just don't sit well with me a.k.a a Gryffindor to the core. So even though some of my favorite characters in books</span>
  <span id="freeText5554459922210189719" style="display:none">First of all ... Newt Scamander I am in love with you. I was already in love with Eddie Redmayne and now this happened and <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1597466933ra/29969870.gif" width="1000" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So ... <i>this book.</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468247919ra/19683415.gif" width="1000" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved the heck out of this. The magic is still there dude. I umm ... don't get along with Hufflepuffs (no offence to all the Hufflepuffs out there. I love you [even though i don't know you]. What i mean is the qualities of the Hufflepuff house just don't sit well with me a.k.a a Gryffindor to the core. So even though some of my favorite characters in books are Hufflepuffs, we rarely get along in real life). But <b>Newt</b> is *dreamy sighs*. He is such a wonderful character who loves his creatures and he gives them names!! He is dedicated to his work and i absolutely adored him. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1597468190ra/29969910.gif" width="1000" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>We have <b>Jacob</b> who is such a cinnamon roll <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1597469032ra/29969987.gif" width="1000" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>and we have <b>Queenie</b> who is so compassionate <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1597469071ra/29969990.gif" width="1000" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>and we have <b>Tina</b> who i don't like (meh)<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1597468694ra/29969945.gif" width="1000" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>and then we have <b>Credence Barebone</b> ... my heart hurts for him. Grindelwald grrrrrrrr<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1597468694ra/29969946.gif" width="1000" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>AND THE MAGICAL CREATURES OH MY GOD YOU GUYS THEY WERE SO AMAZING AND THE <i>CGI EFFECTS</i> AND I WANT A <b>BOWTRUCKLE</b> IN REAL LIFE SO HE CAN HELP ME STEAL GOODIES *evil laugh*<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1597468694ra/29969947.gif" width="1000" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>AND I WANT A NIFFLER SO IT CAN STEAL SHINY THINGS FOR ME AND THEN OUR TRIO WILL CHILLLLLLLLLLLLL.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1597468694ra/29969948.gif" width="1000" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>THAT IS MY DREAM Y'ALL. THAT. <i>THAT</i>. STEAL. EAT. CHILL. READ.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1597468694ra/29969949.gif" width="1000" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>P.S:</b> At the end of this book i was Pickett where i -<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1597468694ra/29969950.gif" width="1000" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>*sigh* Everyone's got attachment issues when it comes to you Newt ❤️️❤️️❤️️<br><br><b>P.P.S:</b> Mary Poppins bag?! I give you Newt Scamander's suticase.</span>

<div id="review_1820752166" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1820752166" />
    <a title="Taylor Knight" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12627819-taylor-knight"><img alt="Taylor Knight" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536879168p2/12627819.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1820752166?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Taylor Knight" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Taylor Knight" href="/user/show/12627819-taylor-knight">Taylor Knight</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30065028-fantastic-beasts-and-where-to-find-them">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12627819-taylor-knight?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12627819-taylor-knight?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12627819-taylor-knight?shelf=best-books-i-read-in-2016">best-books-i-read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1820752166" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15439942711632690341">Even though I was super excited about the Fantastic Beasts movie, I also was a bit hesitant. It's not a secret that I loathed The Cursed Child and I had lost a bit of faith in the wizarding world.<br/>However, Fantastic Beasts (both the movie and screenplay) reminded me of why I love J.K. Rowling's wizarding world so much. <br/><br/>I was very excited to see the wizarding community in America and to see the differences between the two cultures. I loved being able to see the wizarding community in a way that we</span>
  <span id="freeText15439942711632690341" style="display:none">Even though I was super excited about the Fantastic Beasts movie, I also was a bit hesitant. It's not a secret that I loathed The Cursed Child and I had lost a bit of faith in the wizarding world.<br />However, Fantastic Beasts (both the movie and screenplay) reminded me of why I love J.K. Rowling's wizarding world so much. <br /><br />I was very excited to see the wizarding community in America and to see the differences between the two cultures. I loved being able to see the wizarding community in a way that we never got to see in the original 7 books. Harry never really got to experience the wizarding world in the 7 books and neither did the readers. I feel like we really got the chance to see the wizarding world in a new light in Fantastic Beasts. <br /><br />The characters are so bomb. I loved how driven Tina is and how she didn't let Newt sidetrack her from what she thought was the right thing to do. I really loved how her and Queenie worked together and had such a great relationship. They're very different people but they really appreciate each other. <br />Newt is beyond words. He's such a wonderful character (total cinnamon roll, y'all). He loves his creatures so much and will do anything for them, which I loved and related to as well. <br />Don't even get me started on Credence Barebone. His story was so heart breaking and I've never wanted to hug a fictional character so much.<br /><br />Overall, an absolutely wonderful movie and screenplay. It was everything I hoped for and more and I'm so excited for the next movies. I really hope they print the screenplays for the other movies as well and with matching covers because I would love to have the whole series on my Harry Potter shelf.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15439942711632690341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1898076809" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1898076809" />
    <a title="Calista" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16731747-calista"><img alt="Calista" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1436384393p2/16731747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1898076809?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Calista" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Calista" href="/user/show/16731747-calista">Calista</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=award-goodreads-choice">award-goodreads-choice</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-fantasy">genre-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-mystery">genre-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=genre-comedy">genre-comedy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=wordsmith">wordsmith</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=histiorical">histiorical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=myth-folktale-fable">myth-folktale-fable</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=bage-mature">bage-mature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16731747-calista?shelf=series">series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1898076809" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2904613935793402553">This is a script in book form of the movie by the same name. It is interesting and pretty cool to see how a script is written, to read it and then see how that translates to the screen. There aren't as many descriptions, or inner dialogue. We see what they say and do and then we can also read J. K. write about the magic that is happening. I actually like this medium. This is the 2nd script I've read. So, this is what an actor would see. I think that's pretty neat.<br/><br/>I thought this was a great story</span>
  <span id="freeText2904613935793402553" style="display:none">This is a script in book form of the movie by the same name. It is interesting and pretty cool to see how a script is written, to read it and then see how that translates to the screen. There aren't as many descriptions, or inner dialogue. We see what they say and do and then we can also read J. K. write about the magic that is happening. I actually like this medium. This is the 2nd script I've read. So, this is what an actor would see. I think that's pretty neat.<br /><br />I thought this was a great story. It's a story about adults and not really young people. I think some people were missing that connection to a younger crowd. I loved seeing more of J.K's world. She has an endless imagination. She came up with some very cute critters. It sells the story.<br /><br />I think Newt and the rest of the cast are unique and interesting characters. There are few Protagonist out there like Newt. He is rather shy and not that engaging. You sort of have to pry yourself into him and then you grow to love him. We see how deeply he loves and cares for the rare creatures his world is trying to extinguish. <br /><br />My favorite new character is Queeny. She is fantastic. I also think Jacob was funny and rounded out this cast rather well. Tina was my least favorite, such a rule follower, mostly. She has a little bit of Percy Weasley in her, but not as much pompous ass. <br /><br />My favorite new aspect of the world is the Obscurial. That was such an fascinating aspect of the wizarding world. Someone who tries to hide their magic and keep it from coming out can loose their magic so that it's not controllable. They are dangerous and usually emotionally unstable. I love it. I want to see more. <br /><br />There is also a big reveal toward the end that I didn't see coming and it connects the story into the Potterverse.<br /><br />I personally am elated that there are more stories in the Harry Potter world. I haven't heard good things about the 2nd, but I hope it's ok with a strong 3rd book.<br /><br />I found this book well crafted and a lot of fun.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2904613935793402553" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2cYog6F7UdMwJfbXj7SrXoj49EJWlhLZdkxeI3Q+SosC3cuwhyAzIa/9rA0r6BnJ4/Hory1MFPWHOLiH7xK9tA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VATFDNUM8bRxGnhhZJTKCxhwU0g8H1H3vsHcN9y8vxCPHyY/81eTRu7CIrvAyHicc3lPpUfFV9tPtTqTR5BILw==')})
  }

In addition to its own titles, Alfred distributes products from over 50 companies, including Belwin, Daisy Rock Girl Guitars, Dover Publications, DW Drums, Faber Music, Highland/Etling, Kalmus, National Guitar Workshop, Penguin, TASCAM, Ultimate Support, and WEA. All editions are compatible and can be played separately or together. The included CD contains a demonstration of each song followed by a play-along track.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1077326.J_K_Rowling">About J.K. Rowling</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/1077326.J_K_Rowling"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1596216614p3/1077326.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/1077326.J_K_Rowling">J.K. Rowling
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
211,406

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8989242185847757874">See also: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/383606.Robert_Galbraith' title='Robert Galbraith' rel='nofollow noopener'>Robert Galbraith</a><br/>Although she writes under the pen name <b>J.K. Rowling</b>, pronounced like <i>rolling</i>, her name when her first <i>Harry Potter</i> book was published was simply <b>Joanne Rowling</b>. Anticipating that the target audience of young boys might not want to read a book written by a woman, her publishers demanded that she use two initials, rather than her full name. As she had no middle name, she ch</span>
  <span id="freeText8989242185847757874" style="display:none">See also: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/383606.Robert_Galbraith" title="Robert Galbraith" rel="nofollow noopener">Robert Galbraith</a><br />Although she writes under the pen name <b>J.K. Rowling</b>, pronounced like <i>rolling</i>, her name when her first <i>Harry Potter</i> book was published was simply <b>Joanne Rowling</b>. Anticipating that the target audience of young boys might not want to read a book written by a woman, her publishers demanded that she use two initials, rather than her full name. As she had no middle name, she chose <b>K</b> as the second initial of her pen name, from her paternal grandmother Kathleen Ada Bulgen Rowling. She calls herself <b>Jo</b> and has said, "No one ever called me 'Joanne' when I was young, unless they were angry." Following her marriage, she has sometimes used the name <b>Joanne Murray</b> when conducting personal business. During the Leveson Inquiry she gave evidence under the name of <b>Joanne Kathleen Rowling</b>. In a 2012 interview, Rowling noted that she no longer cared that people pronounced her name incorrectly.<br /><br />Rowling was born to Peter James Rowling, a Rolls-Royce aircraft engineer, and Anne Rowling (née Volant), on 31 July 1965 in Yate, Gloucestershire, England, 10 miles (16 km) northeast of Bristol. Her mother Anne was half-French and half-Scottish. Her parents first met on a train departing from King's Cross Station bound for Arbroath in 1964. They married on 14 March 1965. Her mother's maternal grandfather, Dugald Campbell, was born in Lamlash on the Isle of Arran. Her mother's paternal grandfather, Louis Volant, was awarded the Croix de Guerre for exceptional bravery in defending the village of Courcelles-le-Comte during the First World War.<br /><br />Rowling's sister Dianne was born at their home when Rowling was 23 months old. The family moved to the nearby village Winterbourne when Rowling was four. She attended St Michael's Primary School, a school founded by abolitionist William Wilberforce and education reformer Hannah More. Her headmaster at St Michael's, Alfred Dunn, has been suggested as the inspiration for the <i>Harry Potter</i> headmaster Albus Dumbledore.<br /><br />As a child, Rowling often wrote fantasy stories, which she would usually then read to her sister. She recalls that: "I can still remember me telling her a story in which she fell down a rabbit hole and was fed strawberries by the rabbit family inside it. Certainly the first story I ever wrote down (when I was five or six) was about a rabbit called Rabbit. He got the measles and was visited by his friends, including a giant bee called Miss Bee." At the age of nine, Rowling moved to Church Cottage in the Gloucestershire village of Tutshill, close to Chepstow, Wales. When she was a young teenager, her great aunt, who Rowling said "taught classics and approved of a thirst for knowledge, even of a questionable kind," gave her a very old copy of Jessica Mitford's autobiography, <i>Hons and Rebels</i>. Mitford became Rowling's heroine, and Rowling subsequently read all of her books.<br /><br />Rowling has said of her teenage years, in an interview with The New Yorker, "I wasn’t particularly happy. I think it’s a dreadful time of life." She had a difficult homelife; her mother was ill and she had a difficult relationship with her father (she is no longer on speaking terms with him). She attended secondary school at Wyedean School and College, where her mother had worked as a technician in the science department. Rowling said of her adolescence, "Hermione [a bookish, know-it-all <i>Harry Potter</i> character] is loosely based on me. She's a caricature of me when I was eleven, which I'm not particularly proud of." Steve Eddy, who taught Rowling English when she first arrived, remembers her as "not exceptional" but "one of a group of girls who were bright, and quite good at English." Sean Harris, her best friend in the Upper Sixth owned a turquoise Ford Anglia, which she says inspired the one in her books.</span>
